<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Asteroid</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Natural objects within Jupiter's orbit</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Asteroid_(disambiguation)" title="Asteroid (disambiguation)">Asteroid (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

the right), <a href="/wiki/433_Eros" title="433 Eros">433 Eros</a> the first asteroid orbited and landed on (2001) and <a href="/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet)" title="Ceres (dwarf planet)">Ceres</a> a considerably larger asteroid and <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">dwarf planet</a> 1,000 km across.</div></div></div></div>
<p>An <b>asteroid</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Minor_planet" title="Minor planet">minor planet</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Solar_System#Inner_solar_system" title="Solar System">inner Solar System</a>. Sizes and shapes of asteroids vary significantly, ranging from 1-meter rocks to a <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">dwarf planet</a> almost 1000 km in diameter; they are rocky, metallic or icy bodies with no atmosphere.
</p><p>Of the roughly one million known asteroids<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> the greatest number are located between the orbits of Mars and Jupiter, approximately 2 to 4 <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">AU</a> from the Sun, in the main <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_belt" title="Asteroid belt">asteroid belt</a>. Asteroids are generally classified to be of three types: <a href="/wiki/C-type_asteroid" title="C-type asteroid">C-type</a>, <a href="/wiki/M-type_asteroid" title="M-type asteroid">M-type</a>, and <a href="/wiki/S-type_asteroid" title="S-type asteroid">S-type</a>. These were named after and are generally identified with <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">carbonaceous</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metal" title="Metal">metallic</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silica" title="Silica">silicaceous</a> compositions, respectively. The sizes of asteroids varies greatly; the largest, <a href="/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet)" title="Ceres (dwarf planet)">Ceres</a>, is almost 1,000 km (600 mi) across and qualifies as a <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">dwarf planet</a>. The total mass of all the asteroids combined is only 3% that of Earth's Moon. The majority of main belt asteroids follow slightly elliptical, stable orbits, revolving in the same direction as the Earth and taking from three to six years to complete a full circuit of the Sun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-press-kit_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-press-kit-2">[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>Asteroids have been historically observed from Earth; the <i><a href="/wiki/Galileo_(spacecraft)" title="Galileo (spacecraft)">Galileo</a></i> spacecraft provided the first close observation of an asteroid. Several dedicated missions to asteroids were subsequently launched by <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> and <a href="/wiki/JAXA" title="JAXA">JAXA</a>, with plans for other missions in progress. NASA's <i><a href="/wiki/NEAR_Shoemaker" title="NEAR Shoemaker">NEAR Shoemaker</a></i> studied <a href="/wiki/433_Eros" title="433 Eros">Eros</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Dawn_(spacecraft)" title="Dawn (spacecraft)">Dawn</a></i> observed <a href="/wiki/4_Vesta" title="4 Vesta">Vesta</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_Ceres" title="1 Ceres">Ceres</a>. JAXA's missions <i><a href="/wiki/Hayabusa" title="Hayabusa">Hayabusa</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hayabusa2" title="Hayabusa2">Hayabusa2</a></i> studied and returned samples of <a href="/wiki/25143_Itokawa" title="25143 Itokawa">Itokawa</a> and <a href="/wiki/162173_Ryugu" title="162173 Ryugu">Ryugu</a>, respectively. <a href="/wiki/OSIRIS-REx" title="OSIRIS-REx">OSIRIS-REx</a> studied <a href="/wiki/101955_Bennu" title="101955 Bennu">Bennu</a>, collecting a sample in 2020 to be delivered back to Earth in 2023. <i><a href="/wiki/Lucy_(spacecraft)" title="Lucy (spacecraft)">Lucy</a></i>, launched in 2021, has an itinerary including eight different asteroids, one from the <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_belt" title="Asteroid belt">main belt</a> and seven <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_trojan" title="Jupiter trojan">Jupiter trojans</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Psyche_(spacecraft)" title="Psyche (spacecraft)">Psyche</a></i>, to be launched in 2023 or 2024, will study a metallic <a href="/wiki/16_Psyche" title="16 Psyche">asteroid of the same name</a>.
</p><p>Near-Earth asteroids can threaten all life on the planet; an asteroid <a href="/wiki/Impact_event" title="Impact event">impact event</a> resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous%E2%80%93Paleogene_extinction_event" title="Cretaceous–Paleogene extinction event">Cretaceous–Paleogene extinction</a>. Different asteroid deflection strategies have been proposed; <a href="/wiki/Double_Asteroid_Redirection_Test" title="Double Asteroid Redirection Test">Double Asteroid Redirection Test</a> was launched in 2021 and has intentionally impacted into <a href="/wiki/Dimorphos" title="Dimorphos">Dimorphos</a> in September 2022, in an attempt to alter the asteroid's orbit by crashing into it.
</p>

<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Active_asteroids"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Active asteroids</span></a></li>
</ul>
</li>
